كتاب الطلاق أحكام التعليق زوال الملك لا يبطل اليمين، فإن وجد الشرط في الملك طلقت وانحلت، وإلا لا، البقاء محله أي ملك النكاح لا يقع الطلاق وانحلت، وإن اختلفا في وجود الشرط فالقول له إلّا إذا برهنت وما لا يعلَمُ إلا منها . أي الزوجان الزوج أي كل شيء أي من جهتها وزوال الملك إلخ [بعد اليمين بأن طلقها واحدة أو ثنتين وانقضت عدتها(ط) صورته: رجل قال لامرأته: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثم أبانها حتى زال الملك، ثم تزوجها قبل دخول الدار ثم دخلت الدار طلقت؛ لأنه لم يوجد الشرط فيبقى والجزاء باق لبقاء محله، فيبقاء الملك عليها يبقى اليمين والمراد بزوال الملك زواله بطلقة أو طلقتين، أما إذا زال بثلاث طلقات فإنه يبطل اليمين إلا إذا كانت مضافة إلى سبب الملك، فحينئذ لا يبطل بالثلاث كما مر. (مستخلص، عيني) وجد الشرط وهو دخول الدار في قوله: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق". (ع) في الملك: أي ملك النكاح بعد تزوجه مرة أخرى بعد إبانته إياها بعد اليمين. (ع) طلقت وانحلت: أي إن وجد الشرط في الملك أو في حال قيام الملك وقع الطلاق وانحلت اليمين؛ لأن الشرط قد وجد والمحل قابل الجزاء فينزل الجزاء ولا يبقى اليمين؛ لأنه لا بقاء بدون الشرط، وقوله : "وإلا" لا وانحلت" أي وإن لم يوجد الشرط في الملك بل يوجد في غير الملك لم يقع الطلاق؛ لعدم المحلية، وانحلت اليمين لوجود الشرط في غير الملك. وصورته رجل قال لامرأته إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثم أبانها فانقضت عدتها، فدخلت الدار لا يقع شيء، ثم لو تزوجها فدخلت الدار لا يقع شيء أيضاً؛ لأن اليمين قد انحلت بالدخول في حالة البينونة، وإنما قيدنا بانقضاء العدة؛ لأنها لو دخلت الدار في العدة وقع عليها المعلق لما أن البائن لا يلحق البائن إلا إذا كان معلقا فههنا أربع صور فلنصور صورةً جامعة توضح الكل إيضاحاً، هذه: وهي مر ۱ - "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق" فدخلت طلقت وهي صورة وجود الشرط في الملك. ٢- أبالها وانقضت عدتها ثم دخلت الدار لم يقع شيء وهي صورة وجود الشرط في غير الملك. ٣- أبانها ثم دخلها في العدة وقع المعلق أيضاً. ٤ - أبانها وانقضت عدتها ثم تزوجها فدخلت الدار طلّقت، وهي صورة زوال الملك بعد اليمين لا يبطل. (مستخلص) وانحلت أي اليمين يعني انتهت بانتهاء الشرط والجزاء. (ع) وإلا لا : أي وإن لم يوجد الشرط في الملك بأن دخلت الدار بعد الإبانة وانقضاء العدة قبل التزوج بها . (ع) وانحلت أي انتهت اليمين بوجود الشرط. (ع) وجود الشرط: بأن قال الزوج: لم يوجد الشرط أي ما دخلت الدار وقالت: وجد أي دخلتها. (ط،ع) فالقول له: أي للزوج بيمينه؛ لأنه متمسك بالأصل فكان الظاهر شاهدا له؛ لأنه ينكر وقوع الطلاق وهي تدعيه (ع) برهنت: أي إذا أقامت البينة على دعواها فإن القول قولها؛ لأنها نوّرت دعواها بالحجة. (مص،ع) وما لا يعلم إلا منها إلخ: أي وإن علق الرجل طلاق امرأته بشرط لا يعلم إلا من جهتها، فالقول قول المرأة في حق نفسها، وذلك مثل أن يقول: إن حضت فأنت طالق وفلانة معك، أو يقول: "إن كنت تحبيني أو تبغضيني فأنت طالق وفلانة معك"، فقالت المرأة : قد حضت أو أحبك أو أبغضك تطلق هي ولا تطلق فلانة، أما وقوع الطلاق عليها فاستحساناً، والقياس أن لا يقع؛ لأنه شرط وهي تدعي وجود شرط الحنث، والزوج ينكر، فلا تصدق بلا حجة كما لو علق طلاقها بدخول الدار ، وجه الاستحسان: أنها أمينة في حق نفسها والشرط لا يعلم إلا من جهتها، فيجب عليها أن تخبر كي لا يقع في الحرام، فكانت هي متعينة لإقامة الواجب، وهو وقوع الزوج في الحرام، فيجب قبول قولها، وأما عدم وقوع الطلاق على ضرتها؛ فلأن قولها على ضرتها شهادة، وشهادة الفرد غير مقبولة لاسيما إذا كانت متهمة، وهذه إذا كذبها الزوج، أما إذا صدقها تطلق فلانة أيضاً. وإنما يقبل قولها إذاكان الحيض قائماً وقت الخبر، فإذا انقطع لا يقبل قولها؛ لأنه ضروري، فيشترط فيه قيام الشرط، ولو قال: إن كنت تحبيني بقلبك فأنت طالق فقالت: أحبك وهي كاذبة طلقت قضاء وديانة عند الشيخين، وقال محمد لا تطلق ديانة إلا إذا كانت صادقة؛ لأن الأصل في المحبة القلب، واللسان خلف عنه، والتقييد بالأصل يبطل الخلفية ولهما أنه لا يمكن الوقوف على ما في قلبها، فنقل إلى الخلف مطلقاً. واعلم أن التعليق بالمحبة كالتعليق بالحيض لا يفترقان إلا في شيئين: أحدهما: أن التعليق بالمحبة يقتصر بالمجلس؛ لكونه تخييراً، والتعليق بالحيض لا يقتصر على المجلس، ولا يبطل بالقيام كسائر التعليقات والثاني أنها إذا كانت كاذبة في الإخبار تطلق في التعليق بالمحبة وفي التعليق بالحيض لا تطلق ديانة (عيني، مستخلص، فتح) في حقها: أي في حق نفسها لا في حق غيرها. (ط، ع) أو إن كنت أي أو قال لها: إن كنت إلخ. (ع) أو أحبك راجع إلى المسألة الثانية وهي قوله: إن كنت تحبينني. (ع) فقط: دون فلانة وهو جواب المسألتين جميعاً. (ع) لا يقع: أي الطلاق في ما إذا قال لها: إن حضت فأنت طالق، فرأت الدم لا يقع؛ لأنه يحتمل أن تكون مستحاضة فلا يقع بالشك. (ع) ثلاثا : أي ثلاثة أيام مع الليالي. (ط، ع) وقع من حين رأت أي إذا قال لها: إن حضت فأنت طالق فرأت الدم لم يقع الطلاق برؤية الدم حتى يستمر ثلاثة أيام؛ لأن المنقطع دونها لا يكون حيضا بل هو استحاضة، فإذا تمت ثلاثة أيام وقع الطلاق من حين رأت أي من وقت حاضت؛ لأنه عرف بالامتداد أنه من الرحم، فكان حيضا من الابتداء، وفائدته تظهر فيما إذا كانت غير مدخول بها، فإنها لما رأت دماً وتزوجت بزوج آخر واستمر بها الدم ثلاثة أيام كان النكاح صحيحا، وكذا يظهر فيما إذا قال: إن حضت فعبدي حر، والمسألة بحالها كان العبد حراً من حين رأت الدم وكان اكتساب هذه المدة للعبد، وكذا يظهر في الجناية من العبد والجناية عليه في هذه الأيام الثلاثة فإنها تعتبر كجناية الأحرار. (عيني، مستخلص)
Book of Divorce. Rulings on Suspension. Removal of ownership does not invalidate the oath; if the condition occurs in ownership, she is divorced and it is dissolved, otherwise no, the place remains i.e. the ownership of marriage, divorce does not occur and it is dissolved. If they differ about the occurrence of the condition, the statement is his unless she provides proof and what is not known except from her. i.e. the spouses, the husband, i.e. everything, i.e. from her side. 'Removal of ownership etc.' after the oath by divorcing her once or twice and her waiting period ended (ط). Its picture: a man said to his wife: if you enter the house, you are divorced, then he divorced her revocably until ownership ended, then he married her before entering the house, then she entered the house, she is divorced; because the condition did not occur so it remains, and the penalty remains due to the continuation of its place, thus as long as ownership remains on her, the oath remains. The meaning of removal of ownership is its removal by one or two divorces, but if it is removed by three divorces, it invalidates the oath unless it is attached to the cause of ownership, then it is not invalidated by three as previously. (Mukhtasar, Ayni) The condition occurred i.e. entering the house in his statement: if you enter the house you are divorced. (Ayni) In ownership: i.e. ownership of marriage after he married her again after separating her after the oath. (Ayni) She is divorced and it is dissolved: i.e. if the condition occurs in ownership or during the existence of ownership, divorce occurs and the oath is dissolved; because the condition has occurred and the place is suitable for penalty, so the penalty applies and the oath does not remain; because there is no remaining without the condition. His statement: 'otherwise no and it is dissolved' i.e. if the condition does not occur in ownership but occurs outside ownership, divorce does not occur due to lack of suitability, and the oath is dissolved due to occurrence of condition outside ownership. Its picture: a man said to his wife if you enter the house you are divorced, then he divorced her revocably and her waiting period ended, then she entered the house, nothing occurs; then if he marries her and she enters the house, nothing occurs also; because the oath has been dissolved by entry during separation. We specified with expiration of the waiting period because if she entered the house during the waiting period, the suspended divorce would occur because the irrevocably divorced woman is not joined except if suspended. So here are four pictures: 1. 'If you enter the house you are divorced' and she entered, she is divorced - picture of condition occurring in ownership. 2. He divorced her revocably and her waiting period ended, then she entered the house, nothing occurs - picture of condition occurring outside ownership. 3. He divorced her revocably and she entered during the waiting period, the suspended occurs also. 4. He divorced her revocably and her waiting period ended, then he married her and she entered the house, she is divorced - picture of removal of ownership after oath does not invalidate. (Mukhtasar) 'And it is dissolved' i.e. the oath, meaning it ends with the end of condition and penalty. (Ayni) 'Otherwise no' i.e. if the condition does not occur in ownership, by her entering the house after divorce and end of waiting period before marrying her. (Ayni) 'And it is dissolved' i.e. the oath ends by occurrence of condition. (Ayni) 'Dispute on occurrence of condition': i.e. the husband says the condition did not occur i.e. she did not enter the house, and she says it occurred i.e. she entered. (T, Ayni) 'The statement is his': i.e. the husband's with his oath; because he holds the original so the apparent supports him; because he denies occurrence of divorce while she claims it. (Ayni) 'Unless she provides proof': i.e. if she establishes evidence for her claim, then her statement is accepted because she illuminated her claim with proof. (M, Ayni) 'What is not known except from her etc.': i.e. if the husband suspends his wife's divorce on a condition not known except from her side, then the woman's statement is accepted in her own right. For example, if he says: if you menstruate, you are divorced and so-and-so with you, or says: if you love me or hate me, you are divorced and so-and-so with you, and the woman says: I have menstruated, or I love you, or I hate you, she is divorced and so-and-so is not divorced. As for the occurrence of divorce on her, it is by istihsan, and by analogy it would not occur; because it is a condition and she claims occurrence of the condition of breach while the husband denies, so she is not believed without proof as if he suspended her divorce on entering the house. The face of istihsan: she is trustworthy in her own right and the condition is not known except from her side, so she must inform so he does not fall into the forbidden. Thus she is designated to fulfill the obligation, which is the husband falling into the forbidden, so her statement must be accepted. As for the non-occurrence of divorce on her co-wife, because her statement against the co-wife is testimony, and testimony of an individual is not accepted especially if she is biased. If the husband denies her, but if he affirms her, so-and-so divorces also. Her statement is only accepted if menstruation is present at the time of news, if it stops, her statement is not accepted because it is a necessity, so its existence is required. If he said: if you love me in your heart, you are divorced, and she said: I love you, and she is lying, she is divorced judicially and religiously according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: she is not divorced religiously unless she is truthful; because the origin of love is the heart, and the tongue is its deputy, and restriction to the origin invalidates deputyship. For them (the two shaykhs), it is not possible to know what is in her heart, so it is transferred to the deputy absolutely. Know that suspension by love is like suspension by menstruation; they differ only in two things: one: that suspension by love is confined to the sitting because it is a choice, while suspension by menstruation is not confined to the sitting, nor is it invalidated by standing up like other suspensions. The second: that if she is lying in the report, she is divorced in suspension by love, while in suspension by menstruation she is not divorced religiously. (Ayni, Mukhtasar, Fath) 'In her own right': i.e. in her own right not in another's. (T, Ayni) 'Or if you' i.e. or he said to her: if you etc. (Ayni) 'Or I love you' refers to the second issue, i.e. his statement: if you love me. (Ayni) 'Only' i.e. without so-and-so, and it is the answer to both issues. (Ayni) 'It does not occur' i.e. divorce when he said to her: if you menstruate you are divorced, and she sees blood, divorce does not occur; because it is probable that she is mustahada, so it does not occur due to doubt. (Ayni) 'Three' i.e. three days with their nights. (T, Ayni) 'Occurs from when she saw' i.e. if he said to her: if you menstruate you are divorced, and she saw blood, divorce does not occur upon seeing blood until it continues three days; because that which is less than that is not menstruation but istihada. So when three days are completed, divorce occurs from the time she saw, i.e. from when she menstruated; because it is known by its continuous duration that it is from the womb, so it was menstruation from the beginning. Its benefit appears if she was not consummated, for when she saw blood and married another husband and the blood continued three days, the marriage is valid. Likewise in the case where he said: if you menstruate, my slave is free, and the case is similar, the slave becomes free from the time she saw blood, and the earnings of that period belong to the slave. Likewise in the case of a tort committed by the slave or against the slave during these three days, it is considered like the tort of a free person. (Ayni, Mukhtasar)
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on rulings of suspended divorce (talaq mu'allaq). It begins by stating a key principle: removal of ownership (zawaal al-milk) does not nullify the oath of suspended divorce. The condition must occur while the husband still has ownership of marriage (milk al-nikah) for the divorce to take effect. If the condition occurs after ownership has ended (e.g., after irrevocable divorce and expiry of waiting period), the oath is dissolved but no divorce occurs. The commentator then illustrates with four scenarios: (1) condition occurs during marriage – divorce takes effect; (2) condition occurs after irrevocable divorce and expiry of waiting period – no divorce, oath dissolved; (3) condition occurs during the waiting period – divorce occurs because the marriage is still revocable; (4) condition occurs after remarriage – divorce occurs, showing that ownership removal after oath does not invalidate the oath. The discussion then turns to disputes between spouses about whether the condition occurred. The default: the husband's word is taken with oath because he is negating divorce, which is the original state. However, if the wife provides proof, her claim is accepted. For conditions only known by the wife (like menstruation or love), her word alone is accepted for herself, by istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas (analogy), because the condition is hidden and she is trustworthy in her own affairs. Her word is not accepted against a co-wife because that would be testimony, and one witness is insufficient. Finally, the passage discusses the condition of menstruation: it must last three consecutive days to count as hayd; divorce then retracts to when she first saw blood. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted regarding love-based conditions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold that the wife's declaration, even if false, is effective judicially and religiously, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it is only effective religiously if she is truthful. The passage also notes differences between suspension by love and by menstruation.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; abandoning qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling due to necessity or custom.
حيض (hayd): Menstruation; defined as blood that flows for at least three consecutive days and nights (in Hanafi fiqh).
يمين (yamin): Oath; here referring to the suspended divorce declaration itself, which has the force of an oath.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of divorce; stating a condition such that divorce becomes contingent upon its occurrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband suspends divorce on his wife's menstruation. The wife claims she saw blood but it only lasted one day. What is the ruling?
A) She is divorced because her word is accepted by istihsan.
B) She is not divorced because one day of blood is not hayd.
C) She is divorced only if the husband confirms.
D) She is divorced after three days if the blood continues.

Key Takeaway
For hidden conditions known only to the wife, her statement is accepted for herself by istihsan, with specific rules for menstruation (three-day minimum) and a scholarly dispute on love-based suspension (Shaykhayn vs. Muhammad).

The Wife's Claim in Conditional Divorce: Herself vs Co-Wife
Ruling on accepting a woman's claim of condition fulfillment for herself but not for co-wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on accepting a wife's claim of condition fulfillment in a conditional divorce, distinguish between her own case and that of her co-wife, and state the basis of istihsan over qiyas.

Core Idea
A wife's word on a hidden condition is accepted for herself to prevent haram, but not for her co-wife because that would be testimony.

In a conditional divorce (ta'liq), the husband may make divorce dependent on a fact only the wife can know, such as her menstruation or love. How do we determine if the condition occurred? The Hanafi school uses istihsan to accept her word for herself, but not for her co-wife, balancing necessity and testimony rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Understand the conditional divorce formula: 'If you menstruate, you are divorced, and so-and-so (co-wife).' The wife claims the condition occurred. The ruling: she alone is divorced, not the co-wife.
The ruling is based on istihsan, not strict qiyas.
2
State the qiyas (analogy) position
Qiyas would require proof from the wife, just as if the condition were entering a house. Since the husband denies, she would not be believed without evidence. This is the default analogy.
3
Explain the istihsan and its rationale
Istihsan deviates from qiyas because she is trustworthy regarding herself, and the condition is known only to her. Accepting her word is necessary to prevent the husband from remaining in a haram relationship (i.e., with a woman who is actually divorced).
4
Apply the distinction for the co-wife
Her statement about the co-wife is considered testimony (shahada), which is not accepted from a single woman, especially when she has a personal interest (she could be jealous). Therefore, the co-wife is not divorced unless the husband believes her.
5
Note the condition of ongoing menstruation
The wife's claim is only accepted if the menstruation is still present at the time of her report. If it has already ended, her word is not accepted because it is no longer verifiable.
This condition protects against false claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالقول لها في حقها كـ"إن حضت فأنت طالق وفلانة، أو إن كنت تحبينني فأنت طالق وفلانة"، فقالت: حضتُ أو أحبُّك طلّقت هي فقط، وبرؤية الدم لا يقع، فإن استمر ثلاثاً وقع من حين رأت، وفي إن حضت حيضة. الطلاق عليها فاستحساناً، والقياس أن لا يقع؛ لأنه شرط وهي تدعي وجود شرط الحنث، والزوج ينكر، فلا تصدق بلا حجة كما لو علق طلاقها بدخول الدار ، وجه الاستحسان: أنها أمينة في حق نفسها والشرط لا يعلم إلا من جهتها، فيجب عليها أن تخبر كي لا يقع في الحرام، فكانت هي متعينة لإقامة الواجب، وهو وقوع الزوج في الحرام، فيجب قبول قولها، وأما عدم وقوع الطلاق على ضرتها؛ فلأن قولها على ضرتها شهادة، وشهادة الفرد غير مقبولة لاسيما إذا كانت متهمة، وهذه إذا كذبها الزوج، أما إذا صدقها تطلق فلانة أيضاً. وإنما يقبل قولها إذاكان الحيض قائماً وقت الخبر، فإذا انقطع لا يقبل قولها؛ لأنه ضروري، فيشترط فيه قيام الشرط.
So the statement to her regarding her right is like 'If you menstruate then you are divorced, and so-and-so', or 'If you love me then you are divorced, and so-and-so'. She said: 'I menstruated' or 'I love you' – she alone is divorced. And with seeing blood, it does not occur. If it continues for three days, it occurs from the time she saw. And in 'If you menstruate a menstruation'. The divorce upon her is by istihsan, and the analogy is that it does not occur because it is a condition and she claims existence of the condition of violation, and the husband denies, so she is not believed without proof, as if he had suspended her divorce on entering the house. The face of istihsan: she is trustworthy regarding herself, and the condition is not known except from her. So she must inform so that he does not fall into haram. So she is specifically tasked with performing the obligatory, which is preventing the husband from falling into haram. So her statement must be accepted. As for the non-occurrence of divorce on her co-wife, because her statement regarding her co-wife is testimony, and the testimony of a single individual is not accepted especially if she is suspected. And here, if the husband denies her, then if he believes her, so-and-so is also divorced. And her statement is only accepted if the menstruation is present at the time of the report. So if it has stopped, her statement is not accepted because it is necessary, so the condition must be present.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on conditional divorce. It begins with the general principle that when a husband makes a conditional divorce dependent on an act or state that only the wife can know (like menstruation or love), her word is accepted regarding herself. The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), while qiyas would require proof. The reason for istihsan is that it is obligatory for the husband to avoid haram (i.e., being with a woman who is divorced), and the only one who can inform him of the condition's occurrence is the wife. Therefore, her word is trustworthy. However, this applies only to herself. If she claims the condition for a co-wife, it is considered testimony, and a single woman's testimony, especially when she is a potential beneficiary, is not accepted. The exception is if the husband believes her, then the co-wife is also divorced. There is also a condition: the report must be made while the condition (e.g., menstruation) is still ongoing. If it has ended, her word is not accepted because it is no longer verifiable. This protects against false claims.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Conditional suspension of divorce on an event or act.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; deviating from qiyas for a stronger reason.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; here, the wife's statement about her co-wife is treated as testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Qur'an commands believing the wife.
B) Because it prevents the husband from staying in a haram relationship.
C) Because women are always truthful about their bodies.
D) Because the husband has no right to question her.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a wife's unsupported claim of a hidden condition in a conditional divorce to prevent haram, but treats her claim about a co-wife as testimony, which is not accepted.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Conditional Divorce on Love – Qada'an vs Diyanatan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on love conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Shaykhayn and Muhammad regarding a lying wife's divorce in a love conditional, explain the talil behind each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a wife falsely claims love in a conditional divorce, Shaykhayn rule it valid both qada'an and diyanatan; Muhammad rule it only qada'an.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad regarding a conditional divorce based on love. The key question is whether the court's ruling suffices or whether the woman's internal state matters in the sight of God. Understanding this dispute sharpens appreciation of the Hanafi method of talil (reasoning) and the interplay between external and internal dimensions of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Ruling Levels
The husband says: 'If you love me in your heart, you are divorced.' The wife responds 'I love you' but is lying. Note the two dimensions: qada'an (judicially) and diyanatan (religiously).
Qada'an concerns court enforcement; diyanatan concerns the actual ruling in God's sight.
2
State the Positions of Shaykhayn and Muhammad
The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the divorce takes effect both qada'an and diyanatan. Muhammad holds that it takes effect only qada'an; diyanatan it does not take effect unless she is truthful.
Muhammad distinguishes between external enforcement and internal truth.
3
Trace the Talil for Each Position
Shaykhayn: Since the heart is inaccessible, the tongue (the deputy) is the absolute authority. Muhammad: Love resides in the heart; the tongue is merely a deputy; restricting to the original invalidates the deputyship.
The dispute hinges on whether the deputy becomes autonomous when the original is unknowable.
4
Note the Comparison with Menstrual Conditional
The text mentions two differences between love and menstruation conditionals: (1) love is confined to the session (it is a choice), menstruation is not; (2) in love, lying leads to divorce diyanatan, but in menstruation, lying does not.
This comparison clarifies that love conditionals have unique features.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Shaykhayn: the wife is divorced both qada'an and diyanatan even if she is lying. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah; tarjih by al-Marghinani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال: إن كنت تحبيني بقلبك فأنت طالق فقالت: أحبك وهي كاذبة طلقت قضاء وديانة عند الشيخين، وقال محمد لا تطلق ديانة إلا إذا كانت صادقة؛ لأن الأصل في المحبة القلب، واللسان خلف عنه، والتقييد بالأصل يبطل الخلفية ولهما أنه لا يمكن الوقوف على ما في قلبها، فنقل إلى الخلف مطلقاً. واعلم أن التعليق بالمحبة كالتعليق بالحيض لا يفترقان إلا في شيئين: أحدهما: أن التعليق بالمحبة يقتصر بالمجلس؛ لكونه تخييراً، والتعليق بالحيض لا يقتصر على المجلس، ولا يبطل بالقيام كسائر التعليقات والثاني أنها إذا كانت كاذبة في الإخبار تطلق في التعليق بالمحبة وفي التعليق بالحيض لا تطلق ديانة
And if he said: 'If you love me in your heart, then you are divorced' and she said 'I love you' while she is lying, she is divorced both judicially and religiously according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: She is not divorced religiously unless she is truthful, because the original place of love is the heart, and the tongue is a deputy for it. Restricting to the original invalidates the deputyship. Their (the two shaykhs') argument: it is not possible to know what is in her heart, so it is transferred to the deputy absolutely. Know that suspending on love is like suspending on menstruation, except in two matters: one: suspension on love is confined to the session because it is a choice, and suspension on menstruation is not confined to the session and is not invalidated by standing like other suspensions. Second: if she is lying in her report, she is divorced in the suspension on love, but in suspension on menstruation she is not divorced religiously.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute regarding a conditional divorce based on love. When a husband says 'If you love me, you are divorced' and the wife says 'I love you' falsely, the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the divorce takes effect both externally (qada'an) and internally (diyanatan). Imam Muhammad disagrees, holding that it only takes effect externally but not internally unless she is truthful. The reasoning: love is essentially a matter of the heart, which is not accessible. The tongue is merely a deputy. By restricting to the original (the heart), the deputyship is nullified. The two shaykhs argue that since the heart cannot be known, the matter is shifted entirely to the deputy (the tongue). Then the text notes two differences between love and menstruation conditionals: (1) love suspension is confined to the same sitting because it is a choice (takhayyur), whereas menstruation suspension is not confined; (2) in love, if she lies, she is divorced externally and internally, but in menstruation, if she lies, she is not divorced internally (only externally if the husband believes her).

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'an): Judicially; according to the ruling of the court, regardless of inner reality.
ديانة (diyanatan): Religiously; according to what is true in the sight of God, binding in conscience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She is not divorced at all.
B) She is divorced only judicially (qada'an).

D) She is divorced only religiously (diyanatan).

Key Takeaway
When a wife falsely claims love in a conditional divorce, the Hanafi mufta bihi position is that the divorce takes effect both qada'an and diyanatan.

Conditional Divorce on Twin Birth: Qada and Tanazzuh
Ruling on divorce when twins are born and order unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when twins are born and the order of birth is unknown, and explain the distinction between qada'an and tanazzuh.

Core Idea
In ambiguous twin birth, only the minimum certain divorce applies; extra divorces are precaution.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with a conditional divorce scenario where the husband attaches divorce to the sex of the child. When twins are born and the order is unknown, the court applies only the minimum number of divorces that are certain, while extra divorces are taken out of religious caution (tanazzuh). The text also clarifies the effect on the waiting period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional statements
The husband makes two separate conditional oaths: one for a boy (one divorce) and one for a girl (two divorces). Identify each oath as a separate conditional divorce.
2
Recognize the ambiguity
When both conditions are triggered simultaneously (twins) but the order is unknown, we cannot determine which conditional oath was fulfilled first. This creates uncertainty about how many divorces actually occur.
3
Apply the principle of certainty
In Hanafi fiqh, uncertainty is resolved by applying the minimum number that is certain. Here, at least one divorce is certain (since either a boy or girl was born first), so one divorce is applied judicially (qada'an).
The waiting period ends with the birth of the second twin because the 'idda of a pregnant woman ends with delivery.
4
Understand tanazzuh (caution)
To avoid the possibility of sin, additional divorces are taken out of caution (tanazzuh) beyond the judicial minimum. In this case, two divorces are precautionary, bringing the total to three if both were to apply, but only one is legally effective.
Tanazzuh means distancing oneself from areas of potential prohibition.
5
Apply to other combinations
The text extends the ruling to triplets (e.g., boy and two girls, or two boys and one girl) with the same method: apply the minimum certain number judicially and the remainder as caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي إن ولدت ذكراً فأنت طالق واحدة، وإن ولدت أنثى فثنتين، فولدتهما ولم يدر الأوّل تطلق واحدة قضاء وثنتين تنزّها ومضت العدة: [بوضع الحمل؛ لأنه يمينان فأيهما ولدت أولا يحنث به ويقع جزاؤه، فتكون معتدة، وبوضع الثاني تنقضي العدة؛ لأن عدة الحامل تنقضي بالوضع. (ع)] وانحلت اليمين الأخرى بالثاني لوجود الشرط، و لم يقع به شيء؛ لأن الطلاق المقارن بانقضاء العدة لا يقع، وإن علم الأول منهما فلا إشكال فيه وإن اختلفا فالقول قول الزوج؛ لأنه منكر، وإن ولدت غلاماً وجاريتين ولا يدرى الأول يقع ثنتان قضاءً وثلاث تنزهاً. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٥٨/١] والمراد بالتنزه التباعد عن مظان الحرمة ولو ولدت غلامين وجارية يقع واحدة قضاء وثلاث تنزها.
And in [the case of] 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced once, and if you give birth to a girl, twice.' So she gave birth to both and the first is not known: she is divorced once judicially and twice out of caution, and the waiting period passes. And if she gives birth to a boy and two girls and the first is not known, two divorces occur judicially and three out of caution. And if she gives birth to two boys and one girl, one divorce occurs judicially and three out of caution.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on conditional divorce based on the sex of the child when twins are born and the birth order is unknown. The husband's conditional statement creates two separate oaths. When the order is unknown, the divorce is applied to the minimum that is certain judicially, and additional divorces are declared out of religious caution (tanazzuh) to avoid any possibility of sin. The text also explains that the waiting period (idda) ends with the birth of the second child. The principle of tanazzuh means distancing oneself from areas of potential prohibition. The detailed cases show how the ruling applies to different combinations of twins or triplets.

Key Terms
تنزه (tanazzuh): Caution; taking extra steps to avoid potential sin or prohibition.
قضاء (qada'an): Judicially; according to the ruling of the court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a conditional divorce is based on ambiguous birth order, only the minimum certain number of divorces is applied by the court; the remainder is taken as personal religious caution.

Two-Condition Suspended Divorce: When Must Marriage Exist?
Dispute with Zufar on marriage requirement in two-condition suspended divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when marriage must exist in a two-condition suspended divorce and explain Zufar's opposing argument and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
In a two-condition suspended divorce, marriage need only exist when the last condition occurs, not the first.

This lesson examines a specific dispute within the Hanafi school regarding conditional divorce. The question is: if a husband suspends divorce on two conditions (e.g., speaking to two people), does the marriage need to exist at both condition events, or only the second? Zufar argues for both, but the majority Hanafi position requires ownership only at the second condition. We will explore the reasoning behind this view and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Scenario
The husband makes a suspended divorce: 'If you speak to Zayd and Amr, you are divorced three times.' The divorce is conditional on two events.
2
Identify the Hanafi Ruling
The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that marriage must exist only when the second condition occurs. If it occurs within marriage, the divorce takes effect even if the first occurred outside marriage.
3
Understand Zufar's Objection
Zufar argues that both conditions must occur within marriage because they are like one unit, and marriage is required at the time of the second, so also at the first.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
The Hanafis respond that ownership is required only at the time of suspension (ta'liq) to attach the penalty. When the first condition occurs, it is in a state of remaining (baqa'), and ownership is not needed there.
5
Review the Four Scenarios
The text outlines four possibilities: both conditions in marriage (divorce by consensus), both outside (no divorce by agreement), first in marriage and second outside (no divorce except Ibn Abi Layla), first outside and second in marriage (divorce according to Hanafis, contrary to Zufar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والملك يشترط لآخر الشرطين بأن قال لها: إن كلمت زيداً وعمرواً فأنت طالق، فالشرط لوقوع الطلاق أن يكون آخرهما في الملك، فإن وجد الثاني في الملك وقع وإلا لا. صورتها: قال لها: "إن كلمت زيداً وعمراً فأنت طالق ثلاثاً" فطلقها واحدة فانقضت عدتها فكلّمت زيداً وهي مبانة ثم تزوجها فكلمت عمرواً طلقت ثلاثاً الواحدة الأولى أي الواحدة منها وقال زفر: لا يقع حتى يوجد الأول أيضاً في الملك؛ لأن الشرطين كشيء واحد ألا ترى أن الطلاق لا يقع إلا بهما، والملك يشترط عند وجود الثاني فكذا عند الأول، ولنا أن الملك إنما يشترط وقت التعليق ليترتب عليه الجزاء، وحال وجود الشرط الأول حالة البقاء فلا يشترط فيه الملك؛ لاستغنائه عنه في حالة البقاء. والمسألة على أربعة أوجه: إما أن يوجد الشرطان في الملك فيقع ما بقي من الثلاث إجماعاً، أو يوجد في غير الملك فلا يقع ا اتفاقاً، أو يوجد الأول في الملك والثاني في غير الملك فلا يقع إجماعاً إلا عند ابن أبي ليلى، أو وجد الأول في غير الملك والثاني في الملك فتطلق عندنا خلافاً لزفر.
And ownership (marriage) is a condition for the last of the two conditions: that is, if he said to her: 'If you speak to Zayd and Amr, you are divorced.' So the condition for the occurrence of divorce is that the last of them [the condition] be in ownership. If the second is found in ownership, it occurs, otherwise not. Its example: he said to her: 'If you speak to Zayd and Amr, you are divorced three times.' So he divorced her once, and her waiting period ended, then she spoke to Zayd while she was separated (not in marriage), then he remarried her, and she spoke to Amr: she is divorced three times – the first one (i.e., one of them). And Zufar said: It does not occur until the first also occurs in ownership, because the two conditions are like one thing; do you not see that divorce does not occur except by both? And ownership is required at the time of the second, so similarly at the time of the first. Our argument: ownership is required only at the time of suspension [ta'liq] so that the penalty can be attached; and when the first condition occurs, it is in a state of remaining, so ownership is not required at that time because it is not needed in a state of remaining. The issue has four aspects: either both conditions occur in ownership – then what remains of the three divorces occurs by consensus; or both occur outside ownership – then it does not occur by agreement; or the first occurs in ownership and the second outside ownership – then it does not occur by consensus except according to Ibn Abi Layla; or the first occurs outside ownership and the second in ownership – then she is divorced according to us, contrary to Zufar.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in conditional divorce where the husband makes the divorce dependent on two conditions (e.g., speaking to two people). The key ruling is that for the divorce to take effect, the marriage (nikah) must exist at the time the second condition is fulfilled. It does not need to exist at the time of the first condition. This is the Hanafi position, and it is disputed by Zufar, who argues that the marriage must exist at both times because the two conditions are like a single unit. The Hanafi response is that ownership is only required at the time of the original suspension because the purpose is to make the penalty attach; when the first condition occurs, the marriage may no longer exist (e.g., she was divorced after the first condition), but since the suspension remains, the second condition triggers the divorce as long as the marriage is present at that moment. The text then outlines four scenarios to clarify the rule.

Key Terms
ملك (milk): Ownership, here meaning the marriage bond (nikah).
شرط (shart): Condition; the event upon which divorce is suspended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She is not divorced because both conditions must occur in marriage.
B) She is divorced three times.
C) She is divorced only once.
D) She is divorced twice.

Key Takeaway
In a two-condition suspended divorce, the Hanafi school requires marriage only at the time of the second condition, based on the principle that ownership is needed at the moment of suspension attachment.

Conditional Divorce Tied to a Complete Menstruation (Haydah)
Explains when conditional divorce with 'haydah' takes effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce tied to 'haydah' and explain why divorce occurs upon purity, using the hadith of Ali (رضي الله عنه).

Core Idea
A conditional divorce tied to a complete menstruation takes effect only upon purity, not at the onset.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains a specific scenario in conditional divorce: when a husband ties the divorce to his wife's experience of a complete menstruation (haydah). At first glance, one might think the divorce occurs as soon as the bleeding begins. However, the Hanafi school, supported by a hadith from Ali (رضي الله عنه), holds that the divorce only takes effect once the woman becomes completely pure from that menstruation. In this lesson, we will unpack the ruling, its proof, and the precise definition of purity in this context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a conditional divorce (talaq mu'allaq) where the condition is the occurrence of a complete menstruation (haydah). The ruling is that the divorce occurs upon the woman's purification from that menstruation, not at the start.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ali (رضي الله عنه) regarding istibra': 'لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا غير الحبالى حتى يستبرئن بحيضة.'
This hadith requires a complete menstruation for istibra', indicating that haydah is only complete with purity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'حتى يستبرئن بحيضة' shows that the waiting period is based on a complete menstruation. The completion of haydah is defined by its end (purity), so the condition of 'a menstruation' is fulfilled only at purity.
Hanafi scholars derive that haydah is a process that concludes with tuhr.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other madhahib may consider the divorce to occur at the onset of bleeding. The Hanafi school refutes this by insisting on the complete cycle.
This ikhtilaf stems from different interpretations of 'haydah'.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi), as it is consistent with the linguistic and legal definition of haydah and supported by the hadith.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is reported.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقع حين تطهر أي إذا قال لها: إن حضت حيضة فأنت طالق لا تطلق حتى تطهر من حيضها؛ لأن الحيضة الكامل منها وكمالها بانتهائها، وذلك بالطهر؛ لقوله علي: ألا لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا غير الحبالى حتى يستبرئن بحيضة، والطهارة من الحيض بالانقطاع على العشرة أو بمضي العشرة وإن لم ينقطع أو بالانقطاع والاغتسال أو بما يقوم مقام الاغتسال إذا انقطع دون العشرة، وكذلك لو قال: إن حضت نصف حيضة؛ لأنها لا تتجزأ، بخلاف قوله: إن حضت؛ لأنه يدل على الجنس وهو الحيض. (عيني، مستخلص)
It occurs at the time she becomes pure, i.e., if he says to her: 'If you menstruate a menstruation' then she is divorced': she is not divorced until she becomes pure from her menstruation because the complete menstruation is its completion, and its completion is by its end, and that is by purity; due to the statement of 'Ali: 'Beware, pregnant women are not to be approached until they deliver, and non-pregnant until they are made to wait for a menstruation.' Purity from menstruation is by cessation within ten days, or by the passing of ten days even if it does not cease, or by cessation and washing, or by what takes the place of washing if it ceases within ten days. Similarly, if he said: 'If you menstruate half a menstruation,' because it is indivisible, contrary to his saying: 'If you menstruate' because it denotes the genus, which is menstruation. (Ayni, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning conditional divorce tied to menstruation. The author explains that when a husband says to his wife, 'If you experience a menstruation' (haydah), the divorce does not occur until she becomes completely pure (tahir) from that menstruation. The reason is that a complete haydah is only complete at its end, which is when purity begins. This is supported by a hadith attributed to 'Ali (radiyallahu anhu) which instructs that women must be made to wait for a menstruation before intercourse. The passage then details what constitutes purity from menstruation: either cessation within ten days, or the passage of ten days even without cessation, or cessation along with ghusl or its substitute if cessation occurs before ten days. It further states that if the husband says 'half a menstruation,' it is ineffective because menstruation is indivisible (it either occurs or not). This is contrasted with saying 'if you menstruate' without specifying a number, which refers to the genus of menstruation.

Key Terms
الحيضة (al-haydah): A complete menstruation, which is not considered complete until it ends with purity.
الطهر (al-tuhr): The state of purity from menstruation, achieved by cessation within ten days or passage of ten days, or by cessation and ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following methods does NOT establish purity from menstruation?
A) Cessation within ten days
B) Passing of ten days even if bleeding continues
C) Cessation after ten days
D) Cessation within ten days accompanied by ghusl

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a conditional divorce tied to a complete menstruation takes effect only upon the woman's purification from that menstruation, not at its onset.

Conditional Divorce with Twins: Unknown Order
Rulings for conditional divorce when twins are born and order unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for conditional divorce when the order of twins is unknown, distinguishing between judicial ruling (qada') and scrupulousness (tanzih).

Core Idea
When twin births are confused, the court enforces the minimum divorce; the wife observes the maximum out of caution.

This passage addresses the tricky case of conditional divorce where a man says 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced one; if a girl, two.' When twins arrive and the order is unknown, the Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling: only the minimum number of divorces is legally binding, but the wife is advised to observe the higher number to avoid any possibility of sin. The passage also explains how the iddah (waiting period) is completed and how disputes between spouses are resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional statements
The husband made two separate conditional divorces: one for a male child and one for a female child. Recognize that each condition is a separate oath (yamin).
2
Recognize the problem of unknown order
When twins of different sexes are born and the order is unknown, we cannot be certain which condition triggered first. This uncertainty is the core legal issue.
3
Distinguish qada' vs tanzih
Qada' is the judicial ruling based on certainty: the minimum number of divorces that must have occurred (one). Tanzih is a recommendation for scrupulousness: observing the maximum possible (two) to avoid any possibility of violating divine commands.
The text defines tanzih as 'keeping away from areas of prohibition.'
4
Understand iddah calculation
The iddah for a pregnant woman ends with delivery. Upon the first delivery, she enters iddah; upon the second, it ends. The second condition is dissolved but no divorce falls because it coincides with the end of iddah.
5
Apply to other twin scenarios
The passage extends the reasoning to cases where a boy+two girls (order unknown) yield two qada'an and three tanzihan; two boys+one girl yield one qada'an and three tanzihan. Walk through the logic.
The minimum is the number that is certain, the maximum is the highest plausible count.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فولدتهما ولم يدر الأوّل تطلق واحدة قضاء وثنتين تنزّها ومضت العدة بوضع الحمل؛ لأنه يمينان فأيهما ولدت أولا يحنث به ويقع جزاؤه، فتكون معتدة، وبوضع الثاني تنقضي العدة؛ لأن عدة الحامل تنقضي بالوضع. وانحلت اليمين الأخرى بالثاني لوجود الشرط، ولم يقع به شيء؛ لأن الطلاق المقارن بانقضاء العدة لا يقع، وإن علم الأول منهما فلا إشكال فيه، وإن اختلفا فالقول قول الزوج؛ لأنه منكر، وإن ولدت غلاماً وجاريتين ولا يدرى الأول يقع ثنتان قضاءً وثلاث تنزهاً، والمراد بالتنزه التباعد عن مظان الحرمة، ولو ولدت غلامين وجارية يقع واحدة قضاء وثلاث تنزها.
So she gave birth to both and it is not known which was first: she is divorced one (divorce) as a matter of judicial ruling and two as a matter of scrupulousness, and the waiting period passes by the delivery; because there are two oaths, whichever she delivers first, he is subject to its consequence and its penalty falls, so she becomes a waiting woman, and by the delivery of the second the waiting period ends, because the waiting period of a pregnant woman ends by delivery. And the other oath is dissolved by the second due to the existence of the condition, and nothing falls by it, because a divorce concurrent with the end of the waiting period does not fall. And if the first of them is known, then there is no issue. And if they differ, the word is that of the husband because he is the denier. And if she gives birth to a boy and two girls and it is not known which is first, two (divorces) fall as a matter of ruling and three as a matter of scrupulousness. And the meaning of scrupulousness (tanzih) is distancing from areas of prohibition. And if she gives birth to two boys and one girl, one falls as a matter of ruling and three as a matter of scrupulousness.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling for conditional divorce when a wife gives birth to twins (a male and a female) and the order of birth is unknown. The husband had made two conditional statements: 'If you give birth to a male, you are divorced one; if you give birth to a female, you are divorced two.' When both are born, because the true order cannot be determined, the ruling is that one divorce takes effect as a matter of judicial ruling (qada') out of legal certainty, but the woman should observe two divorces out of scrupulousness (tanzih) to avoid any possibility of violating the divine command. The iddah (waiting period) passes with the delivery of both; upon delivery of the first, she enters iddah, and upon delivery of the second, it ends because the iddah of a pregnant woman ends with delivery. The second oath is dissolved by the second birth, but no divorce falls because it would coincide with the end of the iddah. If the order is known, the ruling is straightforward. If there is disagreement between the spouses, the husband's word is taken because he is denying (more divorces). Additional scenarios are given: if she gives birth to a boy and two girls (unknown order), two fall qada'an and three tanzihan; if two boys and one girl, one qada'an and three tanzihan. The term tanzih refers to keeping away from doubtful matters.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'an): As a matter of judicial ruling, based on the certainty of the minimum.
تنزها (tanzihan): As a matter of scrupulousness or religious caution, to avoid doubtful matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
In cases of uncertainty in conditional divorce, the judicial ruling is the certain minimum, but scrupulousness dictates observing the maximum possible.

Ownership Requirement for the Last Condition in Conditional Divorce
Dispute with Zufar on whether ownership is needed at the first condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the requirement of ownership for the last condition in a conditional divorce and explain the practical difference with Zufar's view.

Core Idea
In a conditional divorce with two conditions, only the last condition must occur within the marriage.

The Hanafi school, through Abu Hanifa and his students, developed detailed rules for conditional divorces. One key dispute arises when a husband links two conditions with 'and': does each condition need to occur while the marriage is intact? This passage clarifies that only the final condition requires ownership (being married), while the first can occur even outside the marriage. Understanding this rule resolves many practical scenarios where a first condition occurs during a temporary separation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly that Abu Hanifa (and the majority of the Hanafi school) holds that only the last of the two conjunct conditions must occur within the marriage for the conditional divorce to take effect.
The first condition may occur when the wife is not in the marriage (e.g., during iddah or after a divorce).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar, a student of Abu Hanifa, disagrees. He argues that both conditions must occur while the marriage is intact, because the two conditions are considered as one unit.
Zufar's view is based on the idea that the divorce depends on both conditions equally.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar's proof: the two conditions are like one thing; just as ownership is required at the existence of the second condition, it should also be required at the first. He uses the analogy that the divorce does not occur except by both conditions.
This is a qiyas reasoning: treating the two conditions as a single connected event.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between the time of the conditional utterance and the time the condition occurs. Ownership is needed only at the time of the utterance to attach the consequence. When the first condition occurs, it is a state of continuance (hal al-baqa), and ownership is not required.
The Hanafi school emphasises that the condition is a suspension (ta'liq), not a direct cause.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the first condition occurs before marriage and the second after marriage, the divorce falls according to Hanafi but not according to Zufar. This scenario is explicitly outlined in the passage.
The passage lists four scenarios to illustrate the consensus and disagreement points.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والملك يشترط لآخر الشرطين صورتها: قال لها: إن كلمت زيداً وعمراً فأنت طالق ثلاثاً فطلقها واحدة فانقضت عدتها فكلّمت زيداً وهي مبانة ثم تزوجها فكلمت عمرواً طلقت ثلاثاً الواحدة الأولى أي الواحدة منها وقال زفر: لا يقع حتى يوجد الأول أيضاً في الملك؛ لأن الشرطين كشيء واحد ألا ترى أن الطلاق لا يقع إلا بهما، والملك يشترط عند وجود الثاني فكذا عند الأول، ولنا أن الملك إنما يشترط وقت التعليق ليترتب عليه الجزاء، وحال وجود الشرط الأول حالة البقاء فلا يشترط فيه الملك؛ لاستغنائه عنه في حالة البقاء. والمسألة على أربعة أوجه: إما أن يوجد الشرطان في الملك فيقع ما بقي من الثلاث إجماعاً، أو يوجد في غير الملك فلا يقع اتفاقاً، أو يوجد الأول في الملك والثاني في غير الملك فلا يقع إجماعاً إلا عند ابن أبي ليلى، أو وجد الأول في غير الملك والثاني في الملك فتطلق عندنا خلافاً لزفر. (عيني، مسكين) الشرطين بأن قال لها: إن كلمت زيداً وعمرواً فأنت طالق، فالشرط لوقوع الطلاق أن يكون آخرهما في الملك، فإن وجد الثاني في الملك وقع وإلا لا. (ط،ع)
And ownership is required for the last of the two conditions. Its example: He said to her: 'If you speak to Zayd and 'Amr, you are thrice divorced.' Then he divorced her one and her waiting period ended, then she spoke to Zayd while she was irrevocably divorced, then he married her, then she spoke to 'Amr: she becomes thrice divorced? Actually the text: 'طلقت ثلاثاً الواحدة الأولى' i.e., she is thrice divorced according to the first one. But Zufar said: It does not occur until the first also exists in ownership, because the two conditions are like one thing; do you not see that the divorce does not occur except by both? And ownership is required at the existence of the second, so likewise at the first. Our (Hanafi) argument: Ownership is only required at the time of the conditional statement so that the consequence is attached; the state of the first condition is a state of continuance, so ownership is not required because it is unnecessary in the state of continuance. The issue has four aspects: either both conditions exist in ownership, then the remainder of the three falls by consensus; or they exist outside ownership, then it does not fall by agreement; or the first exists in ownership and the second outside ownership, then it does not fall by consensus except according to Ibn Abi Layla; or the first exists outside ownership and the second in ownership, then she is divorced according to us, contrary to Zufar. (Ayni, Miskin) The two conditions: meaning he said to her: If you speak to Zayd and 'Amr, you are divorced. The condition for the occurrence of divorce is that the latter of them be in ownership. If the second is found in ownership, it occurs; otherwise no. (T., A.)
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the requirement of ownership (being in a valid marriage) for the occurrence of a conditional divorce with two conjunct conditions. The example: The husband says, 'If you speak to Zayd and 'Amr, you are thrice divorced.' The condition is a conjunction of two acts. The Hanafi position, as argued by Abu Hanifa, is that only the last condition needs to occur within the marriage. Zufar argues that ownership is required at both conditions because the two are like one condition. The Hanafi response: Ownership is required only at the time of the conditional statement to attach the penalty; when the first condition occurs, it is a state of continuance so ownership is not required. The discussion outlines four scenarios: (1) both conditions in marriage: divorce falls by consensus; (2) both outside marriage: no divorce by consensus; (3) first in marriage, second outside: no divorce except according to Ibn Abi Layla; (4) first outside, second in marriage: divorce occurs according to Hanafi contrary to Zufar.

Key Terms
الملك (al-milk): Ownership, here meaning the state of being in a valid marriage (the husband's right to divorce).
الشرط (al-shart): Condition; here two conditions linked by 'and'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) In the marriage
B) Outside the marriage
C) Either
D) In the marriage only for the first condition

Key Takeaway
In a conditional divorce with two conjunct conditions, the Hanafi school requires that only the last condition occurs within the marriage for the divorce to take effect.

Immediate Triple Divorce Invalidates a Suspended Triple Divorce
Explains that an immediate triple divorce invalidates a previously sworn conditional triple divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why, in Hanafi law, an immediate triple divorce nullifies a previously conditionally sworn triple divorce, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
An immediate triple divorce exhausts the potential divorce penalty of this marriage, thereby invalidating any prior conditional triple divorce.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqā'iq presents a nuanced scenario: a husband first makes a conditional triple divorce (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced') and then, before the condition occurs, pronounces an immediate triple divorce. The Hanafi school rules that the conditional is nullified. This lesson unpacks the reasoning (based on the nature of the divorce penalty as tied to the current marriage), the analogies with manumission and ẓihār, and the intra-Hanafi disagreement on what happens when the suspended is less than three. By the end, you will be able to apply this principle and understand its underlying usul.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the initial Hanafi ruling
Identify the case: a husband makes a conditional triple divorce (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced') and then pronounces an immediate triple divorce. The Hanafi ruling is that the conditional is invalidated; the wife is irrevocably divorced and the conditional becomes void.
2
Identify the proof (dalil) from the passage
The Hanafi argument: The penalty (jaza') of the oath is the divorces of this specific marriage. Since the immediate triple divorce has already used up all possible divorces of this marriage, there is no remaining penalty to attach to the condition. Hence the oath is void.
This is based on the principle that the divorce penalty is tied to the current marriage.
3
Examine the Hanafi response to Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that the conditional remains because the possibility of occurrence remains after immediate triple (if the wife remarries). The Hanafi response: The condition only applies to this marriage; once the marriage is dissolved by triple, the conditional cannot operate on a future marriage because it was tied to this marriage's divorces.
This highlights the concept of 'mahall' (place) in Hanafi jurisprudence.
4
Compare with the counterexamples of manumission and ẓihār
The text contrasts with a man who conditions freeing his slave and then sells him (oath remains) and a man who conditions ẓihār and then divorces thrice (oath remains). The difference: The 'place' of emancipation is the slave's quality of being a slave, which is not lost by sale; the 'place' of ẓihār is the prohibition of the act, which survives divorce because ẓihār is a prohibition of an act, not of the marriage itself. Divorce, however, prohibits the original permissibility (ḥall aṣlī) of the marriage, and once the marriage ends, the place is gone.
This analogy clarifies why divorce is treated differently.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference regarding divorce less than three
If the suspended was one divorce and the immediate was two, the two shaykhs (Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf) say the suspended is not invalidated; it remains pending. There is a further dispute about the effect of a second husband on less than three divorces: the two shaykhs hold the second husband destroys less than three, while Muhammad holds he does not. This leads to practical differences in whether the wife becomes prohibited after remarriage.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبطل تنجيز الثلاث تعليقه أي تعليق الثلاث على ما يشير إليه أكثر الكتب، والأولى أن يرجع إلى الزوج حتى يشمل تعليق الثلاث وما دونه ولا يخفى أن إضافة المصدر لفاعله الأصل، صورته: أن يقول لامرأته: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثلاثاً ثم نجز الثلاث بطل المعلق حتى لو تزوجها بعد زوج آخر فدخلت الدار لم يقع شيء، وقال زفر: يقع ما علق هو يقول: إن المعلق مطلق الطلاق وقد بقي احتمال الوقوع بعد تنجيز الثلاث، فيبقى اليمين وينزل الجزاء عند الشرط، ونحن نقول: الجزاء طلقات هذا الملك؛ لأن اليمين إنما تعقد لطلاق يصلح جزاء، أما طلقات سيوجد، فلا يصلح جزاء فإذا ثبت تقييد الجزاء بطلقات هذا الملك وقد فاتت بالتنجيز فتبطل اليمين ضرورة. بخلاف ما إذا أبانها بما دون الثلاث؛ لأن الجزاء باق لبقاء محله، فإن قيل: يشكل بما إذا قال لعبده: أنت حر إن دخلت الدار ثم باعه، لا تبطل اليمين مع أن العبد لم يبق محلاً ليمينه، وبما إذا طلقها ثلاثاً بعد ما ظاهر منها منجزاً أو معلقاً بأن قال: إن دخلت الدار فأنت علي كظهر أمي ثم نجز الثلاث تبقى اليمين بالظهار وإن فات المحل حتى لو تزوجها بعد زوج آخر ودخلت الدار صار مظاهرا؟ قلنا: إن العبد بصفة الرق محل للعتق وبالبيع لم تفت تلك الصفة حتى لو فاتت بالعتق لم تبق اليمين والظهار تحريم الفعل لا تحريم الحل الأصلي إلا أن قيام النكاح من شرطه فلا يشترط بقاؤه لبقاء المشروط كالشهود في النكاح، بخلاف الطلاق فإنه تحريم الحل الأصلي وقد فات بتنجيز الثلاث فيفوت بفوات محله وإنما قيد بالثلاث؛ لأنه لو نجز ثنتين بعد التعليق لا يبطل التعليق عند الشيخين أي لو قال لها: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق واحدة ثم نجز طلقتين وانقضت عدتها فعادت إليه بعد زوج آخر ووجد الشرط، فعند الشيخين لا تحرم؛ لأن الزوج الثاني يهدم ما دون الثلاث كما يهدم الثلاث. وقال محمد: إن الزوج الثاني لا يهدم فتعود عنده بما بقي من طلقات الملك الأول، فتحرم عنده حرمة غليظة؛ لأن الثنتين لم تهدما عنده فبقيت واحدة ولما وجد الشرط وقعت الواحدة أيضاً، وأما لو طلقها ثنتين، ثم عادت إليه بعد زوج آخر، وقد كان علّق الثلاث، ثم وجد المعلق عليه طلقت ثلاثاً اتفاقاً، أما عند الشيخين: فلوقوع المعلق كله؛ لأن الزوج الثاني هدم الواقع، وأما عند محمد فلوقوع واحدة من المعلق؛ لأن الزوج الثاني لا يهدم، وقال زفر والشافعي مثل قول محمد (فتح عيني)
And the immediate execution of triple divorce invalidates its conditional suspension, i.e., the conditional triple divorce according to what most books indicate. It is better to refer to the husband so that it includes conditional triple divorce and less. Its form: He says to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced,' then he executes an immediate triple divorce, the conditional is invalidated, such that even if he marries her after another husband and she enters the house, nothing falls. Zufar said: What he conditioned occurs, saying that the conditional is absolute divorce and the possibility of occurrence remains after the immediate triple divorce, so the oath remains and the penalty descends at the condition. But we (Hanafi) say: The penalty is the divorces of this marriage; because the oath is only contracted for a divorce that is suitable as a penalty. But divorces that will exist (in the future) are not suitable as a penalty. So when the penalty is restricted to the divorces of this marriage, and they have been missed by the immediate execution, the oath is necessarily invalidated. Contrary to if he separated her with less than three, because the penalty remains due to the remaining of its place. If it is said: It is problematic with the case where he says to his slave: 'You are free if you enter the house,' then he sells him, the oath is not invalidated even though the slave is no longer a place for his oath; and with the case where he divorces her three after having performed zihar from her, immediate or conditional, as if he said: 'If you enter the house, you are to me like the back of my mother,' then he executes immediate triple divorce, the oath of zihar remains even though the place is lost, such that if he marries her after another husband and she enters the house, he becomes a muzahir? We say: The slave, with the description of slavery, is a place for emancipation, and by sale that description is not lost; if it were lost by emancipation, the oath would not remain. And zihar is a prohibition of the act, not a prohibition of the original permissibility, except that the existence of marriage is a condition for it, so its continuance is not required for the continuance of the conditioned, like witnesses in marriage. Contrary to divorce, because it is a prohibition of the original permissibility and has been lost by the immediate triple divorce, so it is lost by the loss of its place. And it is restricted to triple because if he executes two after the conditional, the conditional is not invalidated according to the two shaykhs. That is, if he said to her: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced one,' then he executes two divorces and her waiting period ends, then she returns to him after another husband and the condition occurs, according to the two shaykhs she does not become prohibited, because the second husband destroys what is less than three just as he destroys three. Muhammad said: The second husband does not destroy, so she returns to him with what remains of the divorces of the first marriage, so she becomes prohibited with a severe prohibition, because the two were not destroyed according to him, so one remained, and when the condition occurred, the one also fell. As for if he divorced her two, then she returned to him after another husband, and he had conditioned three, then the conditioned upon occurred: she becomes thrice divorced by agreement. According to the two shaykhs: because the conditional all occurs because the second husband destroyed the actual. According to Muhammad: because one of the conditional occurs because the second husband does not destroy. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said like the saying of Muhammad. (Fath 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a man first makes a conditional triple divorce (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced') and then, before the condition occurs, he pronounces an immediate triple divorce. According to the Hanafi school (and contrary to Zufar), this invalidates the suspended triple divorce. The reasoning: The suspended divorce is a penalty for this marriage; once the triple divorce has been executed immediately, the potential penalty has already been exhausted, so the suspended one becomes meaningless. The passage compares this to the case of manumission (ʿitq) and zihar to clarify the principle. The discussion also includes the view of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) that if the husband had only one divorce left and then gave an immediate double divorce, the suspended one is not invalidated, unlike triple. There is also a difference of opinion with Muhammad and Zufar/Shafi'i regarding the effect of a subsequent husband after a divorce of less than three.

Key Terms
تنجيز (tanjiz): Immediate execution without condition.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspended or conditional divorce.
محل (maḥall): The legal 'place' or subject matter to which the oath attaches.
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty or consequence that fulfills the conditional oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a previously conditionally sworn triple divorce when the husband later pronounces an immediate triple divorce?
A) The conditional remains valid and will occur if the condition is later fulfilled.
B) The conditional is invalidated and will never occur.
C) The conditional becomes a single divorce.
D) The conditional remains but is reduced to one divorce.

Key Takeaway
An immediate triple divorce nullifies any prior suspended triple divorce because the penalty is exhausted; the same logic does not apply to manumission or ẓihār because their 'place' (maḥall) differs.

Conditional Divorce and Mahr: The Ruling on Staying After Insertion
Ruling on mahr when conditional divorce occurs upon intercourse and the husband stays.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether mahr is due when a conditional divorce/emancipation occurs upon intercourse and the husband remains after insertion, and evaluate the disagreement with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When divorce is conditional on intercourse, mahr is not due for staying; only reinsertion triggers mahr.

This passage addresses a subtle issue in conditional divorce: a husband declares that if he has intercourse, his wife is thrice divorced. He then has intercourse but remains after initial insertion without withdrawing. Is he liable for the mahr? The text clarifies that the divorce occurs at the moment of insertion, and since the marriage ends instantly, the subsequent stay does not create a new obligation for payment. However, Abu Yusuf argues that the entire act constitutes continuous intercourse, so mahr is due. Let us examine the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the conditional declaration
The husband says: 'If I have intercourse with you, you are thrice divorced' (or emancipation for a slave-girl). Then he has intercourse.
The condition is explicitly linked to the act of intercourse.
2
Recognize the key factor: lubth (staying)
After initial insertion, he does not withdraw immediately but remains for some time without separating.
Lubth is defined as remaining after the meeting of circumcised parts without withdrawal.
3
State the ruling according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
No mahr (or 'aqr) is due for a free wife or slave-girl in this situation.
The exception is if he withdraws and reinserts; then mahr becomes wajib.
4
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf argues that the entire act is one continuous intercourse, so mahr is due even without withdrawal.
His proof is that the condition is fulfilled at insertion but the act continues, thus the ongoing contact after divorce should be compensated.
5
Analyze the proof: definition of intercourse
The majority defines intercourse as insertion only – 'idkhal al-farj fi al-farj' – not the duration of staying. Thus the condition is fulfilled at the moment of insertion, the marriage ends, and no subsequent obligation arises.
This definition is the crux of the Hanafi response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو علق الثلاث أو العتق بالوطء لم يجب العقر. علق الثلاث أي الطلقات الثلاث أو البائن. بالوطء: أي بالجماع بأن قال: إن جامعتك فأنت طالق ثلاثاً أو قال لأمته: إن جامعتك فأنت حرة. باللبث: أي بالمكث بعد الإدخال بأن لم يخرجه بعد التقاء الختانين. أي إذا قال لامرأته: إن جامعتك فأنت طالق ثلاثاً أو قال لأمته: إن جامعتك فأنت حرة فجامعها، فلما التقى الختانان مكث ساعة لم يجب عليه المهر إلا إذا أخرجه ثم أدخله فحينئذ يجب المهر، وكذا العقر في الأمة، وعن أبي يوسف: أن المهر يجب عليه في صورة المكث أيضاً؛ لوجود الجماع بالدوام بعد الثلاث وبعد الحرية، ولهما: أن الجماع إدخال الفرج في الفرج =
And if he makes triple divorce or emancipation conditional on intercourse, then the bridal gift (ʿaqr) is not obligatory. He made triple divorce conditional, i.e., the three divorces or the irrevocable divorce. By intercourse: i.e., by copulation, as when he says to his wife: 'If I have intercourse with you, you are thrice divorced' or to his slave-girl: 'If I have intercourse with you, you are free.' By staying (lubth): i.e., by remaining after insertion, such that he does not withdraw after the meeting of the circumcised parts. That is, if he says to his wife: 'If I have intercourse with you, you are thrice divorced' or to his slave-girl: 'If I have intercourse with you, you are free,' then he has intercourse, and when the circumcised parts meet, he remains for a while, the dower (mahr) is not obligatory upon him unless he withdraws and then inserts again; then at that time the dower is obligatory, and similarly the ʿaqr for the slave-girl. And from Abu Yusuf: the dower is obligatory upon him in the case of staying as well, due to the existence of intercourse by continuity after the three divorces and after freedom. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): [that?] intercourse is the insertion of the male organ into the female organ.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage deals with a conditional pronouncement of triple divorce or emancipation tied to the act of intercourse. If a husband says to his wife, 'If I have intercourse with you, you are thrice divorced,' and he has intercourse, then if he remains (lubth) after initial insertion without withdrawing, he is not liable for the mahr (dower), because the divorce or emancipation occurs at the moment of insertion, and the marriage ends at that instant, so no mahr is due for continued contact. However, if he withdraws and reinserts, then the second insertion occurs after the divorce has already taken place (or after she has become free), and so that act would be considered unlawful intercourse, entitling her to mahr (or ʿaqr). Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that the entire act of intercourse, including the prolonged stay, constitutes one act, and since the condition is fulfilled instantly, the remainder is still considered part of the intercourse, so mahr is due. The dominant Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that only the initial insertion triggers the condition, and the subsequent stay does not create liability for mahr because the marriage has already been dissolved. The text ends abruptly, but the key distinction is between a single continuous act and separate acts.

Key Terms
العقر (al-'aqr): The bridal gift or compensation due for intercourse with a slave-girl.
المهر (al-mahr): The dower due to a free wife.
اللبث (al-lubth): The act of remaining after initial insertion without withdrawing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dominant Hanafi view, is a husband obliged to pay mahr if he says 'If I have intercourse with you, you are thrice divorced' and after initial insertion he remains for some time without withdrawing?
A) Yes, mahr is obligatory
B) No, mahr is not obligatory
C) Only half mahr
D) It depends on the duration

Key Takeaway
When a conditional divorce occurs upon intercourse, mahr is not due for staying after initial insertion; only a separate act after withdrawal triggers mahr.

The Nature and Ruling of Exception (Istithna) in Triple Divorce
Explains rulings of conditional divorce, exception, and dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi view on exception in divorce, apply the rules of the ten expressions for conditional divorce, and contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the nature of exception.

Core Idea
Exception in divorce defines the intended count; it is not a retraction but a specification of the remainder.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on exception (istithna) in triple divorce pronouncements. The source passage from Ramz al-Haqa'iq explains the classification of ten expressions used in conditional divorce and delves into a core dispute with the Shafi'i school: does exception redefine the statement or oppose it? Understanding this principle is essential for correctly counting divorces in conditional pronouncements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn ruling on exception
Read the opening ruling: if a husband says 'You are divorced three times except one', two occur; except two, one occurs; except three, three occur. Recognize the pattern.
2
Understand the classification of ten expressions
Learn the four expressions for tamlik (will, intention, love, pleasure) and six for non-tamlik (command, decree, judgment, permission, knowledge, power), and how they interact with prepositions ba, lam, fi.
Refer to the table in the passage.
3
Grasp the Hanafi principle of exception
The core principle: exception is speaking of the remainder (takallum bi al-baqi). The statement from the outset refers to the net amount after exclusion.
4
Examine the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that exception is a preventive opposition (man' al-hukm bi tariq al-mu'arada), like takhsis. Understand his reasoning.
5
Analyse the Hanafi response and thamarah
See the Hanafi rebuttal using Quran and logic. Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) in divorce counting.
In the basic case, both schools may reach the same count, but the underlying theory differs.

وفي "أنت طالق ثلاثاً إلا واحدة تقع ثنتان وفي إلا ثنتين واحدة وفي إلا ثلاثاً ثلاث. أي في قوله لها
